rather than panspermia &#8212; by demonstrating the transformation of inorganic to biological matter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Extremophiles">Extremophiles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panspermia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Extremophiles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Extremophile" title="Extremophile">Extremophile</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1780" data-file-width="1208" decoding="async" height="324" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg/220px-Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg/330px-Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg/440px-Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Blacksmoker_in_Atlantic_Ocean.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hydrothermal_vent" title="Hydrothermal vent">Hydrothermal vents</a> are able to support <a href="/wiki/Extremophile" title="Extremophile">extremophile</a> bacteria on <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a> and may also support life in other parts of the cosmos.</div></div></div>\n<p>Until the 1970s, <a href="/wiki/Life" title="Life">life</a> was thought to depend on its access to <a href="/wiki/Sunlight" title="Sunlight">sunlight</a>. Even life in the ocean depths, where sunlight cannot reach, was believed to obtain its nourishment either from consuming organic detritus rained down from the surface waters or from eating animals that did.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smoker_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-smoker-152">[152]</a></sup> However, in 1977, during an exploratory dive to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galapagos_Rift" title="Galapagos Rift">Galapagos Rift</a> in the deep-sea exploration submersible <i><a href="/wiki/DSV_Alvin" title="DSV Alvin">Alvin</a></i>, scientists discovered colonies of assorted creatures clustered around undersea volcanic features known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_smoker" title="Black smoker">black smokers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smoker_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-smoker-152">[152]</a></sup>  It was soon determined that the basis for this food chain is a form of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bacterium" title="Bacterium">bacterium</a> that derives its energy from <a href="/wiki/Redox" title="Redox">oxidation</a> of reactive chemicals, such as <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">hydrogen</a> or <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen_sulfide" title="Hydrogen sulfide">hydrogen sulfide</a>, that bubble up from the Earth\'s interior. This <a href="/wiki/Chemosynthesis" title="Chemosynthesis">chemosynthesis</a> revolutionized the study of biology by revealing that terrestrial life need not be Sun-dependent; it only requires water and an energy gradient in order to exist.\n</p><p>It is now known that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extremophiles" title="Extremophiles">extremophiles</a>, microorganisms with extraordinary capability to thrive in the harshest environments on Earth, can specialize to thrive in the deep-sea,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LS-20130317_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-LS-20130317-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LS-20130314_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-LS-20130314-154">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NG-20130317_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-NG-20130317-155">[155]</a></sup> ice, boiling water, acid, the water core of nuclear reactors, salt crystals, toxic waste and in a range of other extreme habitats that were previously thought to be inhospitable for life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cavicchioli_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cavicchioli-157">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-adsabs.harvard.edu_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-adsabs.harvard.edu-158">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Surviving_the_Final_Frontier_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-Surviving_the_Final_Frontier-159">[159]</a></sup>  Living bacteria found in ice core samples retrieved from 3,700 metres (12,100&#160;ft) deep at <a href="/wiki/Lake_Vostok" title="Lake Vostok">Lake Vostok</a> in <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a>, have provided data for extrapolations to the likelihood of microorganisms surviving frozen in extraterrestrial habitats or during interplanetary transport.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> Also, bacteria have been discovered living within warm rock deep in the Earth\'s crust.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nanjundiah2000_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nanjundiah2000-161">[161]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In order to test some of these organisms\' potential resilience in outer space, <a href="/wiki/Spermatophyte" title="Spermatophyte">plant seeds</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spores" title="Spores">spores</a> of <a href="/wiki/Endospore" title="Endospore">bacteria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fungus" title="Fungus">fungi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fern" title="Fern">ferns</a> have been exposed to the harsh space environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-adsabs.harvard.edu_158-1"><a href="#cite_note-adsabs.harvard.edu-158">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Surviving_the_Final_Frontier_159-1"><a href="#cite_note-Surviving_the_Final_Frontier-159">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rabbow_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rabbow-162">[162]</a></sup> Spores are produced as part of the normal life cycle of many <a href="/wiki/Plant" title="Plant">plants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">algae</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fungus" title="Fungus">fungi</a> and some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protozoan" title="Protozoan">protozoans</a>, and some bacteria produce <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endospores" title="Endospores">endospores</a> or <a href="/wiki/Microbial_cyst" title="Microbial cyst">cysts</a> during times of stress. These structures may be highly resilient to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ultraviolet_radiation" title="Ultraviolet radiation">ultraviolet</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gamma_radiation" title="Gamma radiation">gamma radiation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Desiccation" title="Desiccation">desiccation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lysozyme" title="Lysozyme">lysozyme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">temperature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Starvation" title="Starvation">starvation</a> and chemical <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disinfectants" title="Disinfectants">disinfectants</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Metabolism" title="Metabolism">metabolically</a> inactive. Spores <a href="/wiki/Germination" title="Germination">germinate</a> when favourable conditions are restored after exposure to conditions fatal to the parent organism.\n</p><p>Although computer models suggest that a captured meteoroid would typically take some tens of millions of years before collision with a planet,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Belbruno2012_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-Belbruno2012-47">[47]</a></sup> there are documented viable Earthly bacterial spores that are 40 million years old that are very resistant to radiation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Belbruno2012_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-Belbruno2012-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC-2011_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-2011-53">[53]</a></sup> and others able to resume life after being dormant for 25 million years,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> suggesting that lithopanspermia life-transfers are possible via meteorites exceeding 1&#160;m in size.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Belbruno2012_47-3"><a href="#cite_note-Belbruno2012-47">[47]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The discovery of deep-sea <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystems</a>, along with advancements in the fields of <a href="/wiki/Astrobiology" title="Astrobiology">astrobiology</a>, observational <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomy</a> and discovery of large varieties of extremophiles, opened up a new avenue in astrobiology by massively expanding the number of possible <a href="/wiki/Planetary_habitability" title="Planetary habitability">extraterrestrial habitats</a> and possible transport of hardy microbial life through vast distances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Experimental_methods_67-4"><a href="#cite_note-Experimental_methods-67">[67]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_in_outer_space">Research in outer space</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panspermia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Research in outer space">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_microorganisms_tested_in_outer_space" title="List of microorganisms tested in outer space">List of microorganisms tested in outer space</a></div>\n<p>The question of whether certain <a href="/wiki/Microorganism" title="Microorganism">microorganisms</a> can survive in the harsh environment of outer space has intrigued biologists since the beginning of spaceflight, and opportunities were provided to expose samples to space. The first American tests were made in 1966, during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gemini_IX" title="Gemini IX">Gemini IX</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gemini_XII" title="Gemini XII">XII</a> missions, when samples of <a href="/wiki/Bacteriophage" title="Bacteriophage">bacteriophage</a> T1 and spores of <i><a href="/wiki/Penicillium_roqueforti" title="Penicillium roqueforti">Penicillium roqueforti</a></i> were exposed to outer space for 16.8 h and 6.5 h, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gerda_Horneck_58-3"><a href="#cite_note-Gerda_Horneck-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Experimental_methods_67-5"><a href="#cite_note-Experimental_methods-67">[67]</a></sup> Other basic life sciences research in <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">low Earth orbit</a> started in 1966 with the Soviet biosatellite program <a href="/wiki/Bion_(satellite)" title="Bion (satellite)">Bion</a> and the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Biosatellite_program" title="Biosatellite program">Biosatellite program</a>. Thus, the plausibility of panspermia can be evaluated by examining life forms on Earth for their capacity to survive in space.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> The following experiments carried on <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">low Earth orbit</a> specifically tested some aspects of panspermia or lithopanspermia:\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="ERA">ERA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panspermia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: ERA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-46_EURECA_deployment.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2820" data-file-width="4316" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/STS-46_EURECA_deployment.jpg/220px-STS-46_EURECA_deployment.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/STS-46_EURECA_deployment.jpg/330px-STS-46_EURECA_deployment.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/STS-46_EURECA_deployment.jpg/440px-STS-46_EURECA_deployment.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-46_EURECA_deployment.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/European_Retrievable_Carrier" title="European Retrievable Carrier">EURECA</a> facility deployment in 1992</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Exobiology_Radiation_Assembly" title="Exobiology Radiation Assembly">Exobiology Radiation Assembly</a> (ERA) was a 1992 experiment on board the <a href="/wiki/European_Retrievable_Carrier" title="European Retrievable Carrier">European Retrievable Carrier</a> (EURECA) on the biological effects of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_radiation" title="Space radiation">space radiation</a>. EURECA was an unmanned 4.5 tonne satellite with a payload of 15 experiments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup>  It was an <a href="/wiki/Astrobiology" title="Astrobiology">astrobiology</a> mission developed by the <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a> (ESA). <a href="/wiki/Spore" title="Spore">Spores</a> of different strains of <i><a href="/wiki/Bacillus_subtilis" title="Bacillus subtilis">Bacillus subtilis</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Escherichia_coli" title="Escherichia coli">Escherichia coli</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Plasmid" title="Plasmid">plasmid</a> <a href="/wiki/PUC19" title="PUC19">pUC19</a> were exposed to selected conditions of space (space vacuum and/or defined wavebands and intensities of solar ultraviolet radiation). After the approximately 11-month mission, their responses were studied in terms of survival, <a href="/wiki/Mutagenesis" title="Mutagenesis">mutagenesis</a> in the <i>his</i> (<i>B. subtilis</i>) or <i><a href="/wiki/Lac_operon" title="Lac operon">lac</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Locus_(genetics)" title="Locus (genetics)">locus</a> (pUC19), induction of <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> strand breaks, efficiency of <a href="/wiki/DNA_repair" title="DNA repair">DNA repair</a> systems, and the role of external protective agents. The data were compared with those of a simultaneously running ground control experiment:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dose_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dose-166">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Horneck_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-Horneck-167">[167]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>The survival of spores treated with the vacuum of space, however shielded against solar radiation, is substantially increased, if they are exposed in multilayers and/or in the presence of <a href="/wiki/Glucose" title="Glucose">glucose</a> as protective.</li>\n<li>All spores in "artificial meteorites", i.e. embedded in <a href="/wiki/Clay" title="Clay">clays</a> or simulated <a href="/wiki/Martian_soil" title="Martian soil">Martian soil</a>, are killed.</li>\n<li>Vacuum treatment leads to an increase of <a href="/wiki/Mutation_frequency" title="Mutation frequency">mutation frequency</a> in spores, but not in <a href="/wiki/Plasmid" title="Plasmid">plasmid</a> DNA.</li>\n<li>Extraterrestrial solar <a href="/wiki/Ultraviolet" title="Ultraviolet">ultraviolet</a> radiation is <a href="/wiki/Mutagen" title="Mutagen">mutagenic</a>, induces strand breaks in the DNA and reduces survival substantially.</li>\n<li>Action <a href="/wiki/Spectroscopy" title="Spectroscopy">spectroscopy</a> confirms results of previous space experiments of a synergistic action of  <a href="/wiki/Vacuum#Outer_space" title="Vacuum">space vacuum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ultraviolet" title="Ultraviolet">solar UV radiation</a> with <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> being the critical target.</li>\n<li>The decrease in viability of the microorganisms could be correlated with the increase in <a href="/wiki/DNA_repair#DNA_damage" title="DNA repair">DNA damage</a>.</li>\n<li>The purple membranes, amino acids and urea were not measurably affected by the dehydrating condition of open space, if sheltered from solar radiation. Plasmid DNA, however, suffered a significant amount of strand breaks under these conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dose_166-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dose-166">[166]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="BIOPAN">BIOPAN</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panspermia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: BIOPAN">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><a href="/wiki/BIOPAN" title="BIOPAN">BIOPAN</a> is a multi-user experimental facility installed on the external surface of the Russian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foton_(space_programs)" title="Foton (space programs)">Foton descent capsule</a>. Experiments developed for BIOPAN are designed to investigate the effect of the space environment on biological material after exposure between 13 and 17 days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kayser_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kayser-168">[168]</a></sup> The experiments in BIOPAN are exposed to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Insolation" title="Insolation">solar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_ray" title="Cosmic ray">cosmic radiation</a>, the space vacuum and weightlessness, or a selection thereof. Of the 6 missions flown so far on BIOPAN between 1992 and 2007, dozens of experiments were conducted, and some analyzed the likelihood of panspermia. Some bacteria, <a href="/wiki/Lichen" title="Lichen">lichens</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Xanthoria_elegans" title="Xanthoria elegans">Xanthoria elegans</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rhizocarpon_geographicum" title="Rhizocarpon geographicum">Rhizocarpon geographicum</a></i> and their mycobiont cultures, the black Antarctic microfungi <i>Cryomyces minteri</i> and <i>Cryomyces antarcticus</i>), spores, and even one animal (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tardigrades" title="Tardigrades">tardigrades</a>) were found to have survived the harsh outer space environment and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmic_radiation" title="Cosmic radiation">cosmic radiation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foton_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-Foton-169">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Foton-M3_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-Foton-M3-170">[170]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tardigrades_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tardigrades-171">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="EXOSTACK">EXOSTACK</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panspermia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: EXOSTACK">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1990_s32_LDEF_stow.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1979" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/1990_s32_LDEF_stow.jpg/220px-1990_s32_LDEF_stow.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/1990_s32_LDEF_stow.jpg/330px-1990_s32_LDEF_stow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/1990_s32_LDEF_stow.jpg/440px-1990_s32_LDEF_stow.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1990_s32_LDEF_stow.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>EXOSTACK on the <a href="/wiki/Long_Duration_Exposure_Facility" title="Long Duration Exposure Facility">Long Duration Exposure Facility</a> satellite.</div></div></div>\n<p>The German <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EXOSTACK" title="EXOSTACK">EXOSTACK</a> experiment was deployed on 7 April 1984 on board the <a href="/wiki/Long_Duration_Exposure_Facility" title="Long Duration Exposure Facility">Long Duration Exposure Facility</a> statellite.  30% of <i><a href="/wiki/Bacillus_subtilis" title="Bacillus subtilis">Bacillus subtilis</a></i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spores" title="Spores">spores</a> survived the nearly 6 years exposure when embedded in salt crystals, whereas 80% survived in the presence of glucose, which stabilize the structure of the cellular macromolecules, especially during vacuum-induced dehydration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gerda_Horneck_58-4"><a href="#cite_note-Gerda_Horneck-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clancy_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-Clancy-173">[173]</a></sup>\n</p><p>If shielded against solar <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UV" title="UV">UV</a>, spores of <i>B. subtilis</i> were capable of surviving in space for up to 6 years, especially if embedded in clay or meteorite powder (artificial meteorites). The data support the likelihood of interplanetary transfer of microorganisms within meteorites, the so-called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lithopanspermia" title="Lithopanspermia">lithopanspermia</a> hypothesis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gerda_Horneck_58-5"><a href="#cite_note-Gerda_Horneck-58">[58]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="EXPOSE">EXPOSE</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panspermia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: EXPOSE">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EXPOSE_location_on_the_ISS.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2029" data-file-width="2918" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/EXPOSE_location_on_the_ISS.jpg/220px-EXPOSE_location_on_the_ISS.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/EXPOSE_location_on_the_ISS.jpg/330px-EXPOSE_location_on_the_ISS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/EXPOSE_location_on_the_ISS.jpg/440px-EXPOSE_location_on_the_ISS.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EXPOSE_location_on_the_ISS.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Location of the astrobiology EXPOSE-E and EXPOSE-R facilities on the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/EXPOSE" title="EXPOSE">EXPOSE</a> is a multi-user facility mounted outside the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a> dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Astrobiology" title="Astrobiology">astrobiology</a> experiments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rabbow_162-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rabbow-162">[162]</a></sup> There have been three EXPOSE experiments flown between 2008 and 2015: <a href="/wiki/EXPOSE#EXPOSE-E" title="EXPOSE">EXPOSE-E</a>, <a href="/wiki/EXPOSE#EXPOSE-R" title="EXPOSE">EXPOSE-R</a> and <a href="/wiki/EXPOSE#EXPOSE-R2" title="EXPOSE">EXPOSE-R2</a>.<br/> \nResults from the orbital missions, especially the experiments <i>SEEDS</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> and <i>LiFE</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LiFE_results_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-LiFE_results-175">[175]</a></sup> concluded that after an 18-month exposure, some seeds and lichens (<i><a href="/wiki/Stichococcus" title="Stichococcus">Stichococcus</a> sp.</i>  and <i><a href="/wiki/Acarospora" title="Acarospora">Acarospora</a> sp</i>., a lichenized fungal genus) may be capable to survive interplanetary travel if sheltered inside comets or rocks from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmic_radiation" title="Cosmic radiation">cosmic radiation</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UV" title="UV">UV</a> radiation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rabbow_162-2"><a href="#cite_note-Rabbow-162">[162]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup>  The <i>LIFE</i>, <i>SPORES</i>, and <i>SEEDS</i> parts of the experiments provided information about the likelihood of lithopanspermia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dirk_Sep2014_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dirk_Sep2014-178">[178]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-R2_retrieval_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-R2_retrieval-179">[179]</a></sup> These studies will provide experimental data to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lithopanspermia" title="Lithopanspermia">lithopanspermia</a> hypothesis,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dirk_Sep2014_178-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dirk_Sep2014-178">[178]</a></sup> and they will provide basic data to <a href="/wiki/Planetary_protection" title="Planetary protection">planetary protection</a> issues.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tanpopo">Tanpopo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panspermia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Tanpopo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stardust_Dust_Collector_with_aerogel.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1909" data-file-width="2103" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Stardust_Dust_Collector_with_aerogel.jpg/220px-Stardust_Dust_Collector_with_aerogel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Stardust_Dust_Collector_with_aerogel.jpg/330px-Stardust_Dust_Collector_with_aerogel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Stardust_Dust_Collector_with_aerogel.jpg/440px-Stardust_Dust_Collector_with_aerogel.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stardust_Dust_Collector_with_aerogel.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dust collector with <a href="/wiki/Aerogel" title="Aerogel">aerogel</a> blocks</div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tanpopo_(mission)" title="Tanpopo (mission)">Tanpopo (mission)</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tanpopo_(mission)" title="Tanpopo (mission)">Tanpopo</a> mission is an orbital <a href="/wiki/Astrobiology" title="Astrobiology">astrobiology</a> experiment by Japan that is currently investigating the possible interplanetary transfer of life, <a href="/wiki/Organic_compound" title="Organic compound">organic compounds</a>, and possible terrestrial particles in low Earth orbit. The Tanpopo experiment took place at the Exposed Facility located on the exterior of <a href="/wiki/Kibo_(ISS_module)" title="Kibo (ISS module)">Kibo module</a> of the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>. The mission collected <a href="/wiki/Cosmic_dust" title="Cosmic dust">cosmic dusts</a> and other particles for three years by using an ultra-low density silica gel called <a href="/wiki/Aerogel" title="Aerogel">aerogel</a>. The purpose is to assess the panspermia hypothesis and the possibility of natural interplanetary transport of life and its precursors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Conference2014_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-Conference2014-181">[181]</a></sup> Some of these aerogels were replaced every one or two years through 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yomiuri_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yomiuri-182">[182]</a></sup> Sample collection began in May 2015, and the first samples were returned to Earth in mid-2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yuko2016_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yuko2016-183">[183]</a></sup> Analyses are ongoing.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panspermia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Panspermia is often criticized because it does not answer the question of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Origin_of_life" title="Origin of life">origin of life</a> but merely places it on another celestial body. It was also criticized because it was thought it could not be tested experimentally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Experimental_methods_67-6"><a href="#cite_note-Experimental_methods-67">[67]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Wallis and Wickramasinghe argued in 2004 that the transport of individual bacteria or clumps of bacteria, is overwhelmingly more important than lithopanspermia in terms of numbers of microbes transferred, even accounting for the death rate of unprotected bacteria in transit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> Then it was found that isolated spores of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B._subtilis" title="B. subtilis">B. subtilis</a></i> were killed by several orders of magnitude if exposed to the full space environment for a mere few seconds. Though these results may seem to negate the original panspermia hypothesis, the type of microorganism making the long journey is inherently unknown and also its features unknown. It could then be impossible to dismiss the hypothesis based on the hardiness of a few earth-evolved microorganism.  Also, if shielded against solar <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UV" title="UV">UV</a>, spores of <i><a href="/wiki/Bacillus_subtilis" title="Bacillus subtilis">Bacillus subtilis</a></i> were capable of surviving in space for up to 6 years, especially if embedded in clay or meteorite powder (artificial meteorites). The data support the likelihood of interplanetary transfer of microorganisms within <a href="/wiki/Meteorite" title="Meteorite">meteorites</a>, the so-called <b>lithopanspermia</b> hypothesis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gerda_Horneck_58-6"><a href="#cite_note-Gerda_Horneck-58">[58]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panspermia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Abiogenesis" title="Abiogenesis"> Abiogenesis</a>&#160;&#8211; The natural process by which life arises from non-living matter</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Anthropic_principle" title="Anthropic principle"> Anthropic principle</a>&#160;&#8211; Philosophical consideration that observations of the universe must be compatible with the observers</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Astrobiology" title="Astrobiology"> Astrobiology</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Astrobiology_(journal)" title="Astrobiology (journal)"> Astrobiology (journal)</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Astrobiology_Magazine" title="Astrobiology Magazine"> Astrobiology Magazine</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cryptobiosis" title="Cryptobiosis"> Cryptobiosis</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Drake_equation" title="Drake equation"> Drake equation</a>&#160;&#8211; Probabilistic argument to estimate the number of alien civilizations in the galaxy</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Earliest_known_life_forms" title="Earliest known life forms"> Earliest known life forms</a>&#160;&#8211; Putative fossilized microorganisms found in hydrothermal vent precipitates</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fermi_paradox" title="Fermi paradox"> Fermi paradox</a>&#160;&#8211; The apparent contradiction between the lack of evidence and high probability estimates for the existence of extraterrestrial civilizations</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fine-tuned_Universe" title="Fine-tuned Universe"> Fine-tuned Universe</a>&#160;&#8211; The proposition that the conditions that allow life in the Universe can occur only when certain universal dimensionless physical constants lie within a very narrow range of values</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Interplanetary_contamination" title="Interplanetary contamination"> Interplanetary contamination</a>&#160;&#8211; Biological contamination of a planetary body by a space probe or spacecraft</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_microorganisms_tested_in_outer_space" title="List of microorganisms tested in outer space"> List of microorganisms tested in outer space</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Planetary_protection" title="Planetary protection"> Planetary protection</a>&#160;&#8211; A guiding principle in the design of an interplanetary mission, aiming to prevent biological contamination of both the target celestial body and the Earth</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rare_Earth_hypothesis" title="Rare Earth hypothesis"> Rare Earth hypothesis</a>&#160;&#8211; Hypothesis that complex extraterrestrial life is a very improbable phenomenon and likely to be extremely rare</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Red_rain_in_Kerala" title="Red rain in Kerala"> Red rain in Kerala</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tanpopo_(mission)" title="Tanpopo (mission)"> Tanpopo (mission)</a>&#160;&#8211; An orbital astrobiology experiment investigating the potential interplanetary transfer of life, organic compounds, and possible terrestrial particles in the low Earth orbit</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tholin" title="Tholin"> Tholin</a>&#160;&#8211; Class of molecules formed by ultraviolet irradiation of organic compounds</li></ul></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Panspermia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-ARX-20171106-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-ARX-20171106_1-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Berera, Arjun (6 November 2017). "Space dust collisions as a planetary escape mechanism". <i>Astrobiology</i>. <b>17</b> (12): 1274&#8211;1282. <a href="/wiki/ArXiv" title="ArXiv">arXiv</a>:<span class="cs1-lock-free" title="Freely
